   Abstract

   The experience of disorientation can be both a hope, for those who
   dream to be elsewhere and a cause for concern, for those who are afraid
   to lose their bearings and refuse to face the otherness of the world.
   Usually, there is change of scenery when there‚Äôs a shift, but it also
   happens that the experience results of a new look at the real. And
   that, away from being a cause of concerns, it encourages to reinvent
   oneself, getting rid of the old self.
